Aid-to-Ma Group Blocked 105

Telegram to the whole country to aid Ma to the death

The Railway Bureau was ordered to dissuade them from going north

The youth's automatic aid-to-Ma anti-Japanese group to the Northeast gathered more than 280 people last night and planned to take the overnight express train to Beijing to go north. The Railway Bureau received a telegram from the Central Government and dissuaded the group from going north. Although the youth of the group were enthusiastic and commendable, they had not received military training in the past. They had no reserves of funds, clothing, grain, and food. Even if they went through hardships, they could not provide any assistance to General Ma Zhanshan when they reached their destination. Therefore, they decided to dissuade them from traveling slowly. At least, they must first telegraph General Ma to report everything and get a reply before they can allow them to proceed. In the future, if there are similar organizations, they will also be strictly dissuaded. The details are recorded below.

Farewell Photo at the North Station (taken by this museum) 106

Meeting in the morning: At 9:00 am, the members of the group living in the South City gathered at the Public Gymnasium on Daji Road in the South City. The head of the group, Zhang Shaojie, gave a speech, saying that he hoped that the members of the group would unite and fight against the violent Japan in order to achieve the true goal of resisting Japan and saving the country. The meeting ended at 10:30 am. At that time, the gathering was discussed.

North Station method: Because it must pass through the concession, it is very inconvenient to walk in teams. Therefore, members of the group were ordered to go to the North Station to gather on their own. The group also prepared twelve tables of meals at the meeting so that members of the group without families could eat in the group. After the meal, they set off to the North Station.

Speech by women representatives from Beiping (Wang Kai Photography) 107

Farewell at the North Station: At 1:00 pm, the members of the group gathered at the North Station. There were more than 100 members of the group. Those who came to the farewell included the China National Road Association, the Beiping Women's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Group, Zhiyi Primary School, the National Lawyers Association, the China Sports School, the Huisheng Midwifery School Rescue Team, the Fazei and United States Schools, the Liangjiang Schools, the Business Press Volunteer Army, the Postal Union Volunteer Army, the Citizens Union Volunteer Army, the South City Volunteer Army, and the North City Volunteer Army. The total number of people farewelling the people was more than 10,000, and the number of volunteers was more than 2,000. A farewell meeting was held. Representatives of the group and various farewell organizations gave speeches that were very sad and solemn, generally saying that they hoped that the aid-to-Ma group would fight against the Japanese pirates and destroy this dynasty. Even if they died on the battlefield in the future, it would be enough to promote the national spirit of our great Republic of China.

Number of departures: There were originally 454 members of the group a few days ago. Because they were going to the Northeast to carry out war, the members of the group were screened. As a result, more than 100 people were weak and could not go to the front line. Therefore, there were more than 320 people. However, only 179 people went to the North Railway Station yesterday, and more than 100 people joined the station temporarily, so there were about 300 people in total. There were two women among them.

Donation of fares: Before the departure, the group contacted the Railway Bureau to take a free ride to no avail. Yesterday, after 1:00 pm, they went to the North Station again because the members of the group were very poor and could not afford to buy it. The people farewelling the group raised a large sum of money to pay for the fares. They donated about 500 yuan. There were those who pledged their clothes on the spot. Chen Weixin, the representative of the Road Association (former mayor of Kaifeng), donated all of his coat and cap and the ten yuan in his pocket. Those who saw it sighed endlessly. The group was able to buy tickets and board the train as usual.

Family farewell: From 1:00 pm to 11:00 pm, when the members of the group gathered at the station, there were wives and young children of the members of the group, or gray-haired old men, who were crying and pulling their clothes, but most of the members of the group refused to cut off their sleeves, and there were also those who were forced by the feelings of their children and temporarily withdrew with tears. Only a very small number said,

Parting words: Huang Jingwan, the director of the association, said to his comrades that the patriotic people from all walks of life thought that the Ma army was isolated, fighting hard and exhausted, and sacrificed everything to resist the violent Japan. Those cowardly troops, hearing of it, could not die in shame. Now I wish the aid-to-Ma group to go and must recover the lost land and save the people of the Northeast from the depths of the water. I hope that the soldiers will return triumphantly and meet each other as soon as possible.

Departure situation: After the group solved the problem of taking the train, it was already 6:00 pm. The head of the group ordered all the members to go to the platform. At that time, more than 10,000 people farewelling the station sent them off with tears. After 7:00 pm, the members of the group boarded the train one after another. At 8:00 pm, they finished boarding the train.

Situation of being blocked: After the aid-to-Ma group boarded the train, they expected to start the train at 12:00 pm last night. The Railway Bureau was ordered to stop the train and notified the group that the overnight express train must be opened first, and then the group's train would be opened later. The members of the group and the volunteers who came to see them off did not believe it and said that the group's train must be opened first before the overnight express train could be opened. The volunteers also sat on the track to prevent being deceived. As of the time this newspaper went to press, there was no news of the train being opened.

Joining from various places: The reporter of Xin Sheng She learned from the group that the people in Zhenxi, Jinghan, and other places had sent letters one after another expressing their willingness to join the departure to the Northeast. The group replied by letter, saying that when the time came, they would wait at the local stations for the group to pass by and join them to go to the Northeast. Therefore, although only 300 people departed in Shanghai this time, there may be thousands of people going to Heilongjiang.

Rear advisory group: Huang Jingwan, Zhao Yaoquan, Tan Bozhao, and other three directors of the group have organized a rear advisory group to take charge of the rear affairs of the group. Because the group is going to the Northeast, the rear work is also very important.

Telegram to the whole country (excerpted above): After thinking repeatedly, we believe that if we sit idly by, we will regret it. We automatically gather patriotic comrades from all walks of life in the country, including farmers, workers, merchants, students, and soldiers, and are determined to sacrifice everything and go to the Northeast to take our blood to aid General Ma and fight against Japan, to win glory for the Chinese nation, and not to be a tool for any faction or any private person, to oppose civil war and the struggle for power and profit among various factions. After joining the group, we must swear with blood. There are already more than 500 participants. It is scheduled to depart from the North Station in Shanghai on December 6. When passing through Beijing, we will hold a parade and demonstration and will not petition the government. We are determined to shed blood outside the Great Wall and expose our bones on the battlefield. Only because the journey is long, the weather is extremely cold, and the number of people is large, our economy is limited. I am afraid that we will become hungry and cold ghosts in the middle of the journey before we reach the battlefield. We have no choice but to ask the patriotic compatriots from all walks of life to donate generously. For the sake of personal integrity, we have specially entrusted the rear advisory group to formulate appropriate measures. All donations should be handed over to the Shanghai Bank and the Hefeng Bank for safekeeping, and then entrusted to the advisory group for donation. We will never spend a penny and live up to the good intentions (excerpted below).

Martial Law in Zhabei Yesterday 108

From 6:00 am to 12:00 pm yesterday, the Fourth and Fifth District Security Bureaus of Zhabei were ordered to enforce special martial law. The police and constables were not allowed to take off their uniforms and were not allowed to go out. Double sentries were added to the important passes, and patrol teams and plainclothes detectives were all deployed. The search of pedestrians with suspicious behavior on the road was very strict. The garrison's patrol was also very serious, with more than ten people in each team, all led by officers.

Telegram for Investigation of Gu Weijun 109

The Municipal Supervisory Committee wired the Central Supervisory Committee, stating: "We submit that Foreign Minister Gu Weijun is betraying the country's interests and violating his oath of office. We respectfully request your review and transfer to the government for immediate dismissal to protect national sovereignty. Our party upholds the late Premier's legacy, advocates for national revolution, and takes down imperialism and abolishes unequal treaties as our sole political program to achieve national freedom, equality, independence, and liberation. Foreign Minister Gu Weijun took office a few days ago, and we firmly believed that he would faithfully abide by our party's political program and engage in revolutionary diplomacy. However, in the recent negotiations with Japan, not only has he failed to advocate for troop withdrawal to protect national sovereignty, but news has also spread that he has voluntarily requested a neutral buffer zone in Jinzhou. He would even be willing to withdraw troops within the Great Wall. Judging from Gu's remarks at the reception for journalists, even with his utmost efforts to gloss over the situation, he could not justify his actions. Troop withdrawal is a prerequisite for all negotiations. The envoy has twice strongly advocated for this in the League of Nations, and the League of Nations has also twice resolved to set a deadline for troop withdrawal. As the League of Nations is meeting again, it should focus on the execution of the previous two resolutions as its sole responsibility. However, it has ignored the troop withdrawal issue and created unnecessary complications, wasting many days to discuss this unnecessary neutral buffer zone issue. If the League of Nations takes this superficial approach, it will automatically indicate its inability to uphold its covenant to restrain the violence to maintain world peace. With no hope for the League of Nations, your country can only seek other avenues or autonomously recover lost territories. There is no need to continue to engage in superficial diplomacy. If the proposal for a neutral buffer zone comes from our envoy, it means that not only has the lost territory in the East not been recovered, but also territory that has not yet been lost is being handed over to international joint management. This is like inviting wolves into the house and opening the door to thieves, surpassing the treachery of Wu Sangui and Shi Jingtang. Furthermore, this resolution allows the Japanese to suppress bandits freely, negating the necessity of the so-called neutral buffer zone, akin to weaving a cocoon to trap oneself, which is alarming. This is one aspect. Recently, the Japanese, insatiable, have been disrupting Tianjin. Our country has used military force to protect our territory and imposed sanctions. If the Japanese attempt to return and cause a war, the responsibility will be theirs, and the blame will fall on them. We have no reason to retreat and concede because we fear their attacks. However, our envoy in the League of Nations proposed to establish an international committee to jointly manage Tianjin. Gu himself did not entirely deny this, but the proposal was rejected by the President of the League of Nations as it fell outside the scope of the topic. This obsequiousness is despicable. Who is responsible for this? All these are the results of the Foreign Minister's dereliction of duty and subservience to foreign powers since taking office. A nation has its supreme sovereignty to protect its territorial integrity. No weak nation should request international joint management of its own territory to undermine its sovereignty. If we request joint management because the Japanese are attacking Tianjin, will we do the same if the Japanese attack Jiangsu and Shanghai? The late Premier stated, 'China's position is second only to that of a colony, where each colony is only ruled by one country, while China is ruled by all countries.' Considering the recent actions of neutrality and joint management, we are further convinced that Gu's betrayal and loss of national sovereignty are heinous crimes. Now, the entire nation is filled with righteous indignation and desires to take desperate measures to avert this crisis. Our National Government still wants to rely on the League of Nations and has not yet taken decisive action. Its prudence and caution are understandable. However, the League of Nations has already declared bankruptcy, and the future of diplomacy is failing.

Even small European and American countries believe that this should not be taken as an example and must be excluded. Yet, Gu Weijun alone believes that the draft resolution of the League of Nations, "although not satisfactory, reduces disappointment." If he has no ulterior motives, he should not be so out of line. His incompetence and shamelessness are obvious. Gu Weijun was previously despised by the people for clinging to warlords and betraying the country. Now, the National Government disregarded his past misdeeds and promoted him in an exceptional manner. He should have strictly adhered to our party's political program and strived to redeem himself. However, he has not done so, but continues his old ways, committing acts of betraying national sovereignty and abandoning our party's political program, which is unforgivable. We request that your committee promptly investigate the Foreign Minister's performance since taking office and forward it to the National Government for immediate dismissal to appease the people and protect national sovereignty. This is in the best interest of the party. Respectfully submitted to the Central Supervisory Committee, Shanghai Special Municipal Supervisory Committee."

The Anti-Japanese Association of University Students. The Anti-Japanese National Salvation United Association of University Students in this city issued a telegram yesterday calling for the dismissal of Gu Weijun, etc. The telegram is recorded as follows: (1) Telegram to the National Government in Nanjing for the Dismissal of Gu Weijun: Foreign Minister Gu Weijun immediately engaged in direct negotiations with Japan, designated Jinzhou as a neutral zone, and suggested that Tianjin be a jointly managed city. This not only violates the government's position of no troop withdrawal and no negotiations, but also places the country in a desperate situation. We hope you will not hesitate, take decisive action, and make a final decision on survival or destruction. We dare to wire you, respectfully requesting your review.

Japanese Residents in China Held a General Meeting Yesterday 112

Resolved on five absurd measures. The concession authorities took strict precautions.

Japanese residents in various parts of China held a general meeting of Japanese residents throughout China at 1 p.m. yesterday to deal with our country's anti-Japanese national salvation movement. Japanese shops in the Hongkou district closed down uniformly in the afternoon to participate. Five measures were resolved. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Temporary Martial Law. The Japanese General Meeting was held at 1 p.m. yesterday in the empty field of the Japanese Central Elementary School at No. 6 Fielun Road. At the entrance of the meeting place, a cloth banner with the words "Japanese Resident General Meeting Throughout China" was written. In front of the meeting place, Japanese urchins distributed national flags to the representatives. The Public Concession Bureau's Political Department was deeply concerned that Japanese rogues would mix in, so it sent a large number of senior Western personnel, together with Chinese and Western armed detectives from the Hongkou Police Station, to impose temporary martial law near Shenjiawan until after the meeting adjourned at 4:20 p.m., and then dispersed.

General Meeting of Japanese Residents (Photo by this Newspaper) 113

Participating Groups: Xiongyuecheng Current Affairs Committee, Changchun Current Affairs Support Association, Changchun Local Office, All-Manchuria Japanese Current Affairs Federation, Support Association for Japanese Current Affairs in Manchuria, Hankou All-Industry Federation, Manchuria Youth League Tieling Branch, Andong Branch, All-Manchuria Empire Veterans Association, South Manchuria Railway Employee Association, Andong County Chamber of Commerce, Fengtian Chamber of Commerce and Industry, Hankou Business Friends Zhizhi Society, Tieling Chamber of Commerce and Industry, All-Shandong Empire Veterans Association, Shanghai, Andong, Suzhou, Hangzhou, Zhifu, Hankou, Shandong, Dalian, Xiamen, Wenzhou, Chongqing, Fuzhou, Yichang, Zhenjiang, Liaoyang, Dashiqiao, Changsha, Beijing, Guangdong, Wuhu, Nanjing, Wanxian, Tianjin, Jiujiang, Shantou, Hong Kong, and other Japanese Resident Associations, totaling forty-three groups. Representatives: Kiyomizu Kihachiro, Hayashi Yuji, Ikeide Shigeo, and more than one thousand Japanese residents in Shanghai. Meeting Details: (1) Setting off firecrackers; (2) Raising the national flag (Japan); (3) Singing songs; (4) Opening remarks; (5) Publicly electing the chairman; (6) Reading the statement and resolutions; (7) Reports from representatives from various regions; (8) Closing remarks. Ikeda Shigeo read the opening remarks, and Hayashi Yuji, chairman of the Shanghai Japanese Chamber of Commerce, was publicly elected as chairman. Miyachi Kanmichi read the resolution.

Representative Speeches: (1) Asada Tanezo: Do not worry about the League of Nations, quickly implement troop increases; (2) Nishikawa Torataro: The truth about the Manchurian Incident; (3) Sato Totaro: Know the principle of cause and effect; (4) Hitomizu Minato: Expel the employers of Manchukuo and Mongolia; (5) Terada Hisanobu: Abolish compromise, hope for a thorough resolution; (6) Oyama Sadato: The great undertaking since the age of the gods; (7) Fukamachi Sakuzō: Diplomacy centered on Manchuria; (8) Fukushima Kisaburo: The ideal of a new Japan; (9) Ozawa Taheiro: The awakening of Japanese people in China; (10) Kiyomizu Kihachiro: Reject weak diplomacy.

Resolutions: (1) The Imperial Government shall firmly secure its rights in Manchuria, protect the lives and property of Japanese people, and take thorough self-defense and security measures; (2) China must fulfill the treaties with the Imperial Government; (3) China must improve its diplomatic attitude and abolish (A) anti-Japanese education and (B) eliminate the slogan "Down with Japanese Imperialism"; (4) Eradicate the anti-Japanese national salvation movement throughout China, and the Imperial Government should take active measures; (5) The Imperial Government should resolve the China problem as a whole and absolutely not allow piecemeal solutions, and reject interference from third parties. Regarding the above five items, the Imperial State regards the situation as serious, and any sacrifice must be carried out to the end. At the same time, the general meeting's statement and resolution were telegraphed to Commander Honjo of the Kwantung Army and Commander Tsude of the Tianjin Fleet.

Absurd Declaration. The reporter from the New Voice News Agency learned many one-sided reasons for its declaration when it adjourned, and the key points are translated as follows: (1) The current conflict between Japan and China is due to the so-called revolutionary diplomatic means of the National Government, which triggered a nationwide anti-Japanese wave. Its internal shortcomings caused the Manchurian Incident and intensified its economic severance with Japan. (2) The revolutionary diplomacy touted by the National Government is to overthrow imperialism, abolish unequal treaties, and constantly implement nationalist xenophobic ideas. Therefore, the Chinese people's feelings towards foreigners are getting worse, or anti-British, or anti-Japanese, and disputes with foreign countries have repeatedly arisen. Coupled with internal strife and chaos, it has reached its extreme. The country has been unable to unify for a long time, warlords have divided the country, and bandits and communists are rampant everywhere. The 400 million people are suffering greatly. The situation in each treaty port is very critical, and China has consistently disregarded international integrity, which can be said to have lost the qualifications of a modern country. (3) Therefore, in order to uphold our Imperial treaty rights, ensure the peace and order of Manchuria, and maintain commercial rights, thorough self-defense measures must be taken. The National Government must have two requirements: (1) Liberate the illegal organizations of the anti-Japanese associations; (2) Eliminate economic severance equal to acts of war and correct its external attitude. (4) In view of the seriousness of the situation in our country, the whole country must be united to deal with the national crisis. Internally, the government authorities must be encouraged, and externally, the truth of the matter must be explained to all countries, thereby achieving a fundamental solution between Japan and China. This is to ensure peace in East Asia.

Deadline for Official Shatian Property to Increase Grain Tax 118

State the reason by the end of the year.

Zhu Yan, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau, issued a proclamation yesterday, stating that in the matter of the official Shatain property households' licenses issued by the Ministry of Finance that have not yet been increased in grain tax and entered into the register, they should request the Bureau to pay the fees for increasing the grain tax and exchange them for land business licenses. The deadline has been stipulated and announced several times, and all have been followed. However, after the deadline, there are still many who submitted the reason for being overdue and requested to handle it with flexibility. It has been verified that the reasons stated are all sincere and can be considered. If we reject them directly, it would not be irrelevant to the original intention of safeguarding people's property, and if we still accept it, how can we treat the households who know that they are overdue and dare not request it? Now, in order to give some flexibility and show great fairness, it is planned that each household that is overdue should submit the reasons for requesting an increase in the overdue grain tax before December 30 of this year, so that the Bureau can review and handle them separately. From January 1, 1921, all overdue documents, no matter what the reasons are stated, will be handled in accordance with the repeated announcements, and no more flexibility will be given in order to emphasize the laws and orders. As for the newly received documents, they should still request an increase in grain tax in accordance with the regulations within six months from the date of receiving the documents. It is urgently announced that all households should abide by it. This proclamation is specially issued.

National Customs' Achievements in Seizing Opium and Morphine 119

According to reports from various Customs Commissioners, the quantities of prohibited items such as opium and morphine seized during the months of July, August, and September of the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931) are as follows:

A total of 251,717 taels and 5 fen of foreign and domestic opium, 5 taels and 5 qian of opium residue, 1,197 taels and 1 qian of morphine, 182 taels and 8 qian of cocaine, heroin, etc., 9 dan and 57 jin of poppy seeds and poppy pods, etc., and various drugs containing toxic substances, estimated to be worth 3,349 taels, 8 qian, 2 fen and 5 li in Customs silver.

Shipping News 120

China Merchants New Steamers Commence Service: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company recently purchased two sea-going steamers from Norway, named "Hai Rui" and "Hai Xiang," each with a load capacity of over 2,700 tons. "Hai Rui" arrived in Shanghai last week, and after completion of repairs, undertook its maiden voyage to Dalian yesterday afternoon. The shipping company's head office has not yet appointed a business director; instead, the position will be filled by the second buyer. It is reported that the "Hai Xiang" also arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and is undergoing minor repairs while customs procedures are being completed. It is expected to join the Northern Seas route as soon as possible.

Recent Situation of Japanese Steamships: Most Japanese steamship companies have voluntarily suspended operations. Although Nippon Yusen, Nisshin Kisen, Osaka Shosen, and Dalian Kisen are still operating as usual, passenger and cargo volumes are greatly reduced. Ships on the Yangtze River route are returning empty, and on the overseas routes, imports into China are nonexistent, and exports are only about one-tenth of their former volume. However, last week, about 20,000 packages of bran and eggs were exported. Among the Chinese traveling to Japan, most are students. The number of Japanese returning to their home country has gradually decreased recently, but groups of three to five people are returning in the name of resident community members on each ship. It is rumored that these Japanese are being sent back by the Japanese consulate and are probably joining the military.

Shanghai-based Zhejiang Shaoxing Gentry Defend Against Cao'e River Floods 123

Organize the Xiaoshun River Dredging Work Relief Committee

Although the floods in the areas near the Cao'e River in Zhejiang Province this year are not as severe as those in Hankou and Gaoyou, the upstream reaches of the river are silted up with mud and sand, making the defenses weak and the danger extreme. If preventive measures are not taken, the consequences will be unimaginable. Shanghai-based Zhejiang Shaoxing gentry have long desired to undertake dredging, but have been unable to do so due to limited funds. Now, with the assistance of the Shaoxing Fellow-Villagers Association, funding has been secured. Therefore, the organizers, including Wang Xiaolai, Song Hanzhang, Feng Zhongqing, Xie Taofu, Yu Futian, Lu Zhimiao, Yan Chengde, Weng Yunhe, Tao Zizhang, Wu Dongsheng, Zhang Jinghan, Gu Zuoxi, and Gong Shaogeng, thirteen people in total, gathered at the meeting room of the Central Trust Company the night before last to discuss how to proceed. On the spot, Wang Xiao was publicly elected as the chairman, and it was decided to name the committee the Xiaoshun River Dredging Work Relief Committee (Cao'e River is also known as Xiaoshun River) to actively carry out the dredging of river sand. However, this work relief effort requires a vast amount of funds, which cannot be accomplished with the few thousand dollars allocated by the Shaoxing Fellow-Villagers Association. It is now planned to organize a fundraising committee to solicit donations widely, so that a little bit can be collected to achieve complete success and make it a permanent solution. It is said that the donation collection point is at the Central Trust Company on Beijing Road, and the association's office is temporarily located at the Shaoxing Fellow-Villagers Association at 26 Avenue Edouard VII.

The Public Works Department Again Discusses Limiting Stalls at Next Year's Jing'an Temple Temple Fair 130

Stallholders Jointly Petition

Jing'an Temple is a scenic spot in Western Shanghai. Every year on the eighth day of the fourth lunar month, which is the celebration of Buddha's birthday, crowds of tourists flock to the area, and thousands of vendors gather to set up stalls, specializing in selling domestically produced goods, creating a grand scene for a time. This year, the Public Works Department proposed limiting the stalls, but after efforts to lobby by Abbot Zhifa of Jing'an Temple, petitions from all stallholders, and assistance from the Social Affairs Bureau, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Citizens' Association, and other organizations, as well as local gentry, the Public Works Department finally withdrew the order to limit stalls and continued to operate according to the old rules. Now, it is heard that the Public Works Department is again discussing limiting the stalls at next year's Jing'an Temple Buddha's birthday celebration. Abbot Zhifa of Jing'an Temple is still firmly lobbying. Upon hearing the news, the stallholders jointly petitioned the Public Works Department. The text of their petition is as follows: "Regarding the petition to withdraw the order to limit the stalls at the Jing'an Temple Buddha's birthday celebration in order to maintain the livelihoods of ordinary people: We, the stallholders, are deeply shocked to hear that your department intends to limit the stalls at the Jing'an Temple Buddha's birthday fair starting next year. This temple fair has been passed down from ancient times and has a history of over a thousand years. Moreover, the former abbot of Jing'an Temple, the late Venerable Zheng Sheng, stipulated in the land lease contract with your department that there would be a Buddha's birthday temple fair where stalls could be set up at will. We, the stallholders, also regard it as a local custom. Every year during the Buddha's birthday, the local villagers gather and sell the local products and tools they have made throughout the year, taking advantage of this opportunity to maintain their livelihood for the year. This is both lawful and beautiful, and it is also in line with the periodic market system of European and American villages. Last year, your department proposed limiting the stalls, but after the Social Affairs Bureau, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Taxpayers' Association, the Citizens' Association, and other legal groups represented the stallholders to petition, and with the petition from the abbot of Jing'an Temple and all the stallholders, the order was finally withdrawn, and the operation continued according to the old rules, for which we were deeply grateful. Now, your department suddenly proposes to implement the restrictions next year, prohibiting many areas that could be used for setting up stalls, which will prevent half of the stallholders from setting up stalls, destroying good customs, and harming the livelihood of ordinary people, which is truly regrettable. Moreover, in the past, many stallholders set up in the middle of the road, but now they have all moved to the cement steps on both sides. In recent years, the roads have been widened, so there is absolutely no obstacle to traffic. This temple fair is also beneficial to society and the local area, and it is best for preserving ancient sites, promoting industry, and customs. We have always admired your department's respect for local relics and its concern for the livelihoods of ordinary people. Therefore, we specifically jointly request that you withdraw the order to limit the stalls in order to maintain the livelihoods of tens of thousands of people in Western Shanghai. We would be extremely grateful. Respectfully submitted to Mr. Mackie, Director-General, and Mr. Ho, Commissioner, of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession."

Number of Inmates at the Caohijing Prison Increases to Over Two Thousand 131

Lighter Criminals Temporarily Suspended from Imprisonment

To Be Executed in the Detention Center

In recent years, the population of this city has increased sharply, and the quality of people has become uneven. Therefore, the number of criminals has also increased sharply. When the Second Jiangsu Prison in Caohijing was built, the original quota was for accommodating 800 prisoners. Although the original quota was sometimes exceeded due to the rotation of prisoners in and out, there was no concern about overcrowding. The original quota for the detention center of the local court was only 300 people, and the prisoners were also more comfortable. However, since last year to this year, in one corner of the Chinese area, the Public Security Bureau has been sending criminals to the court every day, always exceeding a hundred people. At the same time, there are also direct accusations to the court, and those who are released after paying fines are still not a few. Therefore, there are often six to seven hundred people in the detention center. Fortunately, the detention center built a new cell block in the fifteenth year, so there is no panic about not being able to accommodate everyone. However, it is already feeling very crowded. However, once a criminal conviction is finalized, they are sent to prison. Therefore, the court must send twenty to thirty prisoners to the Second Prison for execution every morning, which has led to a sharp increase in the number of inmates in the prison to over two thousand, which is three times the original quota, causing a panic about overcrowding. Currently, Warden Dong Changmin has considered building additional cells on the remaining land, but construction cannot begin due to lack of funds. However, the later prisoners really cannot be accommodated anymore. Therefore, he submitted a request to the High Court to ask for a relief method. On the one hand, he consulted with President Shen and Chief Prosecutor Liu of the Local Court to temporarily suspend sending prisoners for execution to the prison in order to alleviate the situation. It is now heard that the High Court has ordered that criminal prisoners sentenced to more than three months of imprisonment should still be sent to prison for execution, while those sentenced to less than three months can be executed in the detention center, because those with short sentences are easier to be released.

A Rascal Sells His Wife into Prostitution 132

A Deposit of Four Hundred Yuan Has Been Paid Wife Discovers Plot and Writes to Her Brother for Rescue

All Parties Involved Are Detained Awaiting Sentencing

Hua Sun, a woman from Changzhou residing at No. 135 Weituoma Road, is 29 years old and has some beauty. Her husband, Hua Fusheng, from Wuxi, does not engage in proper work and spends his time with dissolute people, leading to an empty wallet. On the 23rd of last month, on the pretext of taking his wife to the Great World to play, he colluded with He A Si and Gao A Gen from Suzhou to sell Ms. Hua to Wu, a woman from Guangxi Road, Fuzhi Lane, No. 11, for 400 yuan. 14 yuan was paid as a deposit, and the rest would be paid after the boat to Shantou arrived and Ms. Sun was taken there to work as a prostitute. After the voyage, the money would be cleared. After Ms. Sun temporarily resided at Wu's place, she heard that she was going to Shantou to work as a prostitute. Because the journey was long and there would be no day to return home, she took the opportunity to write to her brother, Sun Zhiqing. After receiving the letter, Sun was extremely shocked and reported the matter to the Yangshupu Police Station the day before yesterday. Detective Ma Zonglai went to arrest Hua, He, and Gao and went to No. 11 Fuzhi Lane on Guangxi Road to rescue Ms. Hua Sun, while Wu had already escaped upon hearing the news. Hua Fusheng and the others were taken to the police station and detained. Hua Sun was taken back by her brother. The next morning, they were sent to the First Special Court, High Division 1. According to the police station lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, the statement of the case was presented, and it was requested that the case be investigated. According to Hua Sun's statement, she married the defendant Hua Fusheng as his wife in August of last year. At that time, he tricked her into going to the Great World and Tianyunlou to play. They went to a certain inn to stay overnight. The next day, they wrote a paper in the room of the New Hotel on Jiujiang Road. At that time, He A Si and Gao A Gen were also present and sent to Ms. Wu's place. Hua Fusheng (her husband) said he was going to Shantou to look for business. Later, she learned that she was going to be a prostitute, so she wrote a letter to inform her brother. The police detective came and rescued her, etc. According to the testimony of her brother, Sun Zhicheng, Hua Fusheng confessed that the matter was his wife's voluntary choice to go to a foreign port to be a prostitute, but the rest of his testimony was ambiguous. He A Si confessed that Ms. Hua's sale into prostitution was arranged by Hua Fusheng and Gao A Si in advance and that he was not the mastermind. Gao A Si confessed that Hua Fusheng discussed with him that he wanted to buy his wife as a prostitute, and he said it was not possible and that he needed to find a job for a female worker who could also earn money. Lawyer Fan Gang was also hired for defense. Judge Xiao Xie fen ordered the three defendants to be detained pending sentencing.

Woman Accuses Man of Abandonment after Seduction 133

Requests Alimony of Over 20,000 Yuan

Shi Jupao, a woman from Changshu, is now 20 years old. She has recently hired a lawyer to sue Shao Demao (aka De Mao), who resides at 366 Taian Lane, North Shaanxi Road, in the First Special District Court, for abandonment after seduction, requesting a judgment ordering the payment of alimony, etc. Her petition states that in February of this year, through the introduction of Xu Wu bao, she married the defendant as a concubine and lived together at 62.5 Jing'an Lane on Longmen Road. The defendant paid expenses of about 200 yuan per month. This lasted for five months. The plaintiff suddenly fell ill and was bedridden. The defendant initially showed signs of disgust in his words, and then disappeared completely. The love of the past was all in vain. The plaintiff was so irritated that the illness worsened. Fortunately, her elderly mother was by her side to take care of her and provide treatment. After several months, she finally recovered, but she had mortgaged almost everything and had no way to borrow money. Therefore, she entrusted lawyer Jiang to send a letter to inquire, but the defendant ignored it. Having no choice, she filed a criminal lawsuit, which was not accepted. The plaintiff is a weak woman with heavy responsibilities to support her elders and raise her younger siblings. Now that she has been lured away and then abandoned, if the court does not order the defendant to pay alimony, how will she maintain her livelihood? Therefore, she requests that the court order the defendant to pay 20,000 yuan in alimony, 2,000 yuan in tea money, and about 3,000 yuan for living and medical expenses. The case was heard the day before yesterday by Judge Guo Shouyi in Civil Court 7. The defendant, Shao Demao, hired lawyers Wu Linkun and Wang Fushang to defend him, saying that the plaintiff was a prostitute named Hui Xia Lao Ba, then changed her name to Yang Yuanyuan Lao Ba, and now is named Lu Lan Lao Ba. The defendant met the plaintiff in the Yang Yuanyuan brothel, where the plaintiff was still an assistant (commonly known as a follower). Later, the defendant would call for Yang Yuanyuan whenever he needed to socialize in a brothel, and the plaintiff would always follow. There is a book of Yang Yuanyuan's records that can be checked. Later, the plaintiff moved to Jing'an Lane. The defendant was completely unaware at first. Later, the plaintiff entrusted Ni Tianbiao to copy down the address and come forward, claiming that the plaintiff's business was sparse and begging the defendant to help invite guests. The defendant refused politely. On the tenth day of the fifth lunar month, he met the plaintiff on the road, who said that she had only earned over 40 yuan in Yang Yuanyuan's place last month, which was not enough for shoes and socks. If there were no clients to help, she would have no face to return to the brothel and begged the defendant to take on the opening act. The defendant agreed casually and then suddenly received a letter from a lawyer, named Shi, whom the defendant did not know. The defendant returned the letter. The defendant's claim that he had a marital relationship with her is completely false. On November 26th, the defendant's friend, Chen Youqing, hosted a banquet at the Hongyun brothel on Shantou Road and called for Lu Lan, and the plaintiff also followed. If given some time, the defendant will be able to find considerable evidence to prevent the plaintiff from denying it, and the defendant has never lived with the plaintiff. How can she obtain the status of a concubine? Then, the unreasonableness of her demand can be seen in its entirety. He should request that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed and that the plaintiff be ordered to bear the costs of the case, etc. Judge Guo checked the arguments and announced that the debate in this case was concluded and that the sentencing was scheduled.

Shen Yingxiang of Zhihe Bank Is Sued Again 134

Qu Hongsheng's 30,000 Yuan Missing

Accuses Shen of Breach of Trust and Damage to Savings

After the Zhihe Yongji Bank closed down, the deficit was quite large. Many cases in which the manager of the bank, Shen Yingxiang, was sued by various creditors in court have also occurred. Recently, Qu Hongsheng hired lawyer Ni Gang to file a complaint with the First Special District Court accusing Shen Yingxiang, the manager of Zhihe Yongji Bank, of breach of trust, etc. The petition states that the plaintiff had 30,000 taels of silver in savings in Zhihe Yongji Bank, managed by the defendant Shen Yingxiang. On August 20th of this year, the bank suddenly closed down, and Shen Yingxiang disappeared without a trace. He originally intended to sue, but he learned that Gan Jiji, a creditor of the bank, had already filed a criminal lawsuit and that the court had issued a warrant for Shen's arrest, and he had been arrested and brought to court to post bail for liquidation. Therefore, he did not proceed with the lawsuit. Now, he has learned that after the defendant was released on bail, he did not prepare to repay his debts and planned to flee again, which further shows that on the day before the defendant closed down, he colluded with his son, Shen Chengfu, to issue promissory notes and withdraw hundreds of thousands of taels in cash, intending to abscond with the money. The circumstances are very clear. The defendant, as the manager of Zhihe Bank, intended to gain illegal benefits for himself and committed an act of breach of trust in his duties, causing damage to the plaintiff's savings, which constitutes the crime of breach of trust under Article 366 of the Criminal Code. Therefore, he has filed a lawsuit requesting the immediate arrest of the defendant Shen Yingxiang and a legal investigation. The court approved the petition and ordered a summons. The defendant failed to appear for questioning the day before yesterday. The plaintiff's representative, lawyer Ni Gang, stated the case. The judge stated that since the defendant had not appeared, there was no way to proceed, and he ordered that the date be changed and that the defendant be summoned again for questioning.

A Young Woman from a Good Family Abducted to Hankou and Forced into Prostitution 135

The Abductor Was a Close Friend of Her Husband

She Was Able to Escape After the Guards Let Down Their Guard

Cai Jinyun, a chauffeur from Haimen who resides at No. 7 Yudeli, Penglai Road in the Chinese Concession, married Wang Xiuzhen (19 years old this year), a woman from Suzhou, in March of last year. On April 28th of this year, she suddenly disappeared, only returning home on the 14th of last month. According to her, Yang Amao, a chauffeur from the Public Security Bureau (from Nantong), colluded with Cai Ziqing, Zhang Asan, and others to abduct her to Hankou to become a prostitute, but failed. After returning to Shanghai, she was again imprisoned in a brothel and forced into prostitution. Cai learned of the situation, and the couple jointly entrusted a lawyer to file a lawsuit with the Second Special District Local Court, accusing Yang and the other two, as well as Zhang Jinhu and his wife Mao Xiangchun, Zhang Xinjie, the female proprietor Sheng Asheng, and others – a total of eight people – of enticing and raping her. The day before yesterday afternoon, the court summoned both parties, and Ge Zhiqin, the presiding judge of the criminal court, opened the first criminal court to hear the case. The judge first questioned the ages, origins, and occupations of the plaintiff and defendants. Only Yang Amao and his lawyer appeared in court; the rest were absent. The judge ordered Cai Jinyun and the witness Cai Jinzhou to leave the courtroom. According to Cai Wang Xiuzhen's testimony, the defendant Yang Amao was in the same profession as her husband and a close friend, often visiting her house. On the afternoon of April 28th of this year, Yang Amao came to her house and said that her husband was at the Gonghe Inn in Tangjiawan, calling her to go there. Believing this to be true, she went with him but did not find her husband. She was then imprisoned inside. That night, she was sexually assaulted by Yang Amao and Cai Ziqing. The next morning at seven o'clock, they took her to room number four of the Pingjiang Inn on Sanma Road and imprisoned her, forbidding her to make a sound. On the 30th, they drew up a document and paid money, and Mao Xiangchun took her to Hankou to force her into prostitution. She was beaten when this failed. In May, they brought her back to Shanghai, first residing at No. 94 Huai'anli, Baker Road. In August, they moved her to Zhang Jinhu's house at No. 196 Glock Road in the French Concession, forcing her into prostitution and having people guard her. On the morning of the 14th of last month, the guards let down their guard, and she escaped to the iron gate of Fangbanqiao, where she met her husband's brother, Cai Jinzhou, who took her home. She told her husband and in-laws the whole story and filed a lawsuit, etc. The judge ordered Cai Jinyun to appear in court. According to his testimony, his wife disappeared on April 28th of this year, and he reported it to the Second Branch of the Second District Public Security Bureau. When his wife returned home, he learned that she had been abducted by Yang and the others. The witness is in the same profession and a friend of Yang. The rest of his testimony was similar to what Xiuzhen said. The witness Cai Jinzhou testified that Cai Jinyun is his cousin. At eleven o'clock in the morning on November 14th, he met his sister-in-law on Huacheng Road and took her home. He did not know the circumstances before or after. The defendant Yang Amao denied the abduction and rape, stating that he had never visited Cai Jinyun's house and that he was being framed. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that the second defendant, Cai Ziqing, had been arrested by the plaintiff and detained in the Public Security Bureau in the Chinese Concession four or five days ago. He requested that he be transferred to the court for questioning. The addresses of the remaining four, seven, eight, and three defendants are correct, but they have not been served with summons. He requested that arrest warrants be issued. Both parties reside in the Chinese Concession, but because the crime occurred under the jurisdiction of this court, the lawsuit was filed here. The judge then ordered the plaintiff couple to leave and asked the witness Cai Jinzhou whether his sister-in-law and the defendant Yang Amao had any contact on weekdays. Cai replied that he lived separately and never interfered in their affairs. After his sister-in-law returned home, she told him that she had been raped by Yang. The plaintiff Cai Jinyun also stated that the second defendant Cai Ziqing was arrested by his younger brother and taken to the Second Branch of the Second District Public Security Bureau. At this point, it was already dusk, and the judge adjourned the hearing to the afternoon of December 12th, when Cai Ziqing would be brought in, and Zhang Jinhu and others would be arrested and further questioned. The court was then adjourned.

Burglary 136

Residents Must Be Careful

At the home of He Yaozu, located at No. 1 Jimao Alley, Qinglong Bridge in the Nanshi area, at around 11:00 AM yesterday, just as the family was preparing to have lunch, they suddenly heard a loud pounding on the door. When they asked who it was, a voice outside said they were there to visit Mr. He. As soon as they opened the door, three tall men strode in. Without asking any questions, they pulled out guns and threatened the family into silence. The He family realized they were being robbed and were terrified. One of the robbers went into the downstairs bedroom and stole gold jewelry and other items worth several hundred yuan. They then went upstairs, intending to search for more valuables. However, the robbers were afraid of taking too long and attracting attention, so they hurriedly abandoned their search, went downstairs, gathered their accomplices, and fled with the stolen goods. As they left, they fired a shot into the air as a show of force.

Jiangbei Woman Picking Up Old Bamboo 141

Beaten by a Colleague, Breaking Her Leg

Seems A Little Too Cruel

The piles of bamboo ends in front of the Yuantai Bamboo Shop on Dithwei Road in Hongkou are often stolen. On the morning of the day before yesterday, at around 5:00 AM, Gu Zhushi, a woman from Jiangbei, was walking past the entrance of the bamboo shop and picked up several old bamboo pieces, intending to take them back for firewood. Guan Xiufang, a colleague from Nanxiang, saw this and grabbed the woman, using a thick bamboo root to strike her leg. Bicycle Kills a Person 142

Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Compensated 500 Yuan

Dai Afeng, a Suzhou native who lives at 61 Mafang Alley, Longmen Road and plays the trumpet, was riding a bicycle from south to north on Avenue Lieutenant Peten in the French Concession at around 1:00 PM on the 30th of last month, crossing Avenue Edward VII when he hit Zhu Zhiquan, a Shaoxing native (52 years old, a medicinal herb merchant), causing head injuries and death. The police detained Dai and sent him to the Second Special Court for questioning. Yesterday, he was interrogated again. Police lawyer Gu Shouxi stated that the north-south lights were red at the time, and the defendant violated traffic regulations by crossing the road, resulting in the death of a person. He is now prosecuting him under Article 291 of the Criminal Law and Article 4 of the Traffic Regulations, requesting an investigation. Police officer Lu Yongtian, badge number 368, also reported the situation of the defendant's violation of traffic regulations at the time of the accident. Zhu Luo Shi, the wife of the deceased, stated that her husband was tragically killed in the accident and that she has four young and old family members who have no means of support. She requested that the defendant be ordered to compensate her for damages to maintain her livelihood. The defendant confessed that the north-south lights were red that day, and he wanted to turn east, but he was stopped by the police, causing the car to rush north and cause the accident. He stated that he has an elderly mother and is very poor, pleading for leniency. Judge Ge Zhiqin reviewed the confession, ordered the police lawyer to make arguments, and declared the trial closed. Dai Afeng was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for the crime of causing death due to negligence. The number of days of detention before the verdict was allowed to be deducted, and he was ordered to compensate Zhu Luo Shi for damages of 500 yuan.

Record of the General Meeting of Creditors of Wang Yi Bank 150

The General Meeting of Creditors of Wang Yi Bank held its second meeting yesterday at the Lixin Accountants' Office at 452 Jiangxi Road. About 80 creditors attended the meeting. First, Pan Xulun, the temporary representative chairman, reported on the resolutions of the first and second meetings of the temporary representatives, as well as the progress of handling creditor registration and verifying the accounts of Wang Yi Bank. Then, the entire temporary representative group resigned. The creditor representatives present publicly elected Pan Xulun as the temporary chairman and resolved the following important matters: (1) Elect five official representatives by ballot; (2) The elected officials will first contact Wang Yi Bank to discuss methods of repaying creditors, and then convene a meeting of creditors after receiving a satisfactory response. Bai Chengde is Harmed by Car Thieves 152

Bai Chengde, a native of Gaoyou who currently resides at Yongxiang Building, west of the bridge next to Xuejiawan Road in Nanshi, used to farm in his hometown to support himself. This autumn, his fields were flooded, and he had no way to make a living. He came to Shanghai alone and was introduced by a fellow villager to pull a rickshaw at the home of Wang Rongqing, a native of Yancheng, at 126 Huiguan Street. Because the floods in various counties in Jiangbei were widespread, the number of people hiring rickshaws at Wang's house, both old and new, was much higher than in previous years. Although the income was limited, it was better than starving to death. Therefore, Bai Chengde came to Shanghai for several months, but the actual time he spent pulling a rickshaw was less than a month, and his life was extremely difficult. Yesterday, he repeatedly pleaded with the rickshaw owner, who gave him rickshaw license number 4317 to operate. Unexpectedly, when he arrived near Xieqiao, two men, appearing to be workers, sat down in a rickshaw that had been pre-hired, and one temporarily hired Bai's rickshaw, claiming to be foremen who wanted to find workers on Linyin Road. They chatted with Bai about his family life as they went along, behaving as if they were very close to him. Before long, they got out of the rickshaws, looking around and pretending to be looking for someone. They stopped and started several times. When they reached a certain alley on Linyin Road, they both got out of the rickshaws and told Bai to go inside and get the fare. The other rickshaw puller volunteered to watch the rickshaws, and told Bai to bring the money with him. Bai suspected something was wrong, and when he came out, both the men and the rickshaws were gone. He went into the alley to look for the passengers, but they had already escaped by another route. There are several cases of theft and fraud like this every day in the Chinese Concession. The loser has to prepare 15 or 16 yuan to redeem the original rickshaw. The rickshaw owner had repeatedly warned him about this, but Bai was tricked by the thieves. It is extremely unfortunate. He is now wandering on the streets day and night, searching for his lost rickshaw. His situation is extremely pitiful.

Reader Correspondence

To All Readers Who Communicate with Letters 154

Fight, defend, or make peace?

Your letters unanimously advocate for war, and the intensity of your excitement has reached a boiling point. At the same time, you vehemently criticize Zhang Xueliang's non-resistance and the central government's unwavering reliance on the League of Nations, which is ineffective and painless, and what you are especially worried about is the government's tendency to compromise with Japan.

In fact, what we advocate is not war, but defense. When the enemy attacks, we should do our best to resist and not let them cross the line. This is defense. Even if defense leads to war, it can only be called a defensive war. Zhang Xueliang's crime of non-resistance is the crime of not defending.

The way to establish a country is first to be able to defend. Only by being able to defend can one advance to fight or retreat to make peace. If the enemy attacks Shenyang, then defend Shenyang. If the enemy attacks Jilin, then defend Jilin. If the enemy attacks Jinzhou, then defend Jinzhou. If the enemy attacks Tianjin, then defend Tianjin. The local military authorities are responsible for defending the territory. If the enemy comes, they should naturally defend without needing to ask for instructions from senior officials or the central government. If they can do this, the enemy will have no weaknesses to exploit and will naturally be discouraged and return home. This is our only hope, and this is our only advocacy.

Even if a certain place is taken advantage of by the enemy, if the first line of defense cannot be held, then defend the second line of defense. If the second line of defense cannot be held, then defend the third line of defense. If you really exert all your strength and retreat only when your strength is exhausted, the enemy will definitely not dare to underestimate you, and the people will also be moved by your righteousness and be happy to provide support. Look at the results of Ma Zhanshan's hard fighting. Although Qiqihar eventually fell, Japanese newspapers wrote about it in great detail, expressing their admiration. Aid from all sides is still pouring in. The total strength of Zhang Xueliang's troops inside and outside the Guan is more than dozens of times that of the officers under Ma Zhanshan's isolated army in the Hei province. Is it really that there is no one like Ma Zhanshan? Is the ease with which the rear provides supplies not comparable to the remote corner of the Hei province? If on September 18, 19, 20, 21, etc., you held the city firmly, fought to the death, and never retreated, after a certain period of time, there would be international support. Even if Shenyang and Jilin were eventually lost due to the pressure of the enemy's troops, the Japanese would not treat us as incompetent as they do today and act recklessly. The people would treat Zhang Xueliang as they treat Ma Zhanshan, so that the reputation of China and the dignity of the nation, although defeated, would still be glorious, and it would not necessarily be a complete defeat. If we take a defensive posture and not an offensive posture, how can the Japanese side accuse us of starting a war?

Let's not talk about the past, let's talk about the future. What we ask of the government is defense. If they attack Jinzhou, then defend Jinzhou. Why rush to agree to劃立中立區 [establish a neutral zone]? If they attack Tianjin, then defend Tianjin. Why automatically request that all countries jointly manage it? Could it be that if they attack the capital, they will also ask all countries to jointly manage the capital?

This request cannot be said to be forcing someone to do something difficult. The country supports an army of 2 million men, and the people bear the cost of 400 million yuan a year to support the army. If we can't even defend, how will the government face the people of the whole country?

If you say you can do it, then why rush to compromise? On the one hand, stand firm, on the other hand, declare that you will adopt Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant to cut off commercial relations and prohibit all exchanges between people. After six months or even a year, let's see how Japan changes.

Readers, what we ask of the government is just one word: "defend." But what is the latest news? Have you paid attention to the following news items in yesterday's newspaper?

(1) Shi Zhaoji sent a note to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, explaining China's position on the withdrawal of troops to within the Great Wall and the execution of police duties in the neutral zone. The Nanjing government's position has not changed in any way, but it recognizes that the neutral zone has several indispensable formalities attached.

(2) The Secretary-General of the League of Nations notified all members of the information obtained from Minister Shi. This information is mostly about the negotiations between Chinese Foreign Minister Gu and other key figures in the Nanjing government regarding the status of Jinzhou.

(3) The Japanese army's withdrawal to Shenyang is because the Chinese have taken the initiative to withdraw their troops into the Guan. Now, if we reject the establishment of a neutral zone, it is proof that China has broken its promise. If this news is true, can we still say that the government has not tended towards compromise? Please pay attention.

Postal Stamp 155

Affix this stamp and the appropriate amount of postage when sending letters.

Weather Report 156

The Xujiahui Observatory predicted yesterday at 4:30 PM that the lower Yangtze River region and northern Jiangsu would be cloudy and unsettled, with fog and thunderstorms, due to a low-pressure system passing through and moving northeast. Cyclones here and in the Yellow Sea are strengthening, and the winds in the East China Sea are strong and unpredictable. In the south of the China Sea, the weather is severe, and the center of the hurricane was approximately 12 degrees north latitude and 117 degrees east longitude, within 120 miles of the intersection, heading west at 2:00 PM yesterday. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 67.2 and the lowest was 45.5, compared to the highest of 55.0 and the lowest of 37.2 on the same day last year.

The Voice of Resistance Against Japan 157

— The Impoverished Swordsman of Yun

In the first month of the sixteenth year of the Guangxu reign, Yang Zitong, the Chinese envoy to Russia, became seriously ill in the Russian capital and eventually passed away. The Russian King and Queen sent officials to express their condolences, and their sentiments were gracious and generous. Subsequently, the "睰哇" (Transliteration: possibly "Nova") newspaper of that country obtained a telegram from Tokyo, Japan, stating that a certain Japanese newspaper claimed that Envoy Yang had been pushed from an upper floor by Russians, leading to his death. The chief editor of "睰哇" newspaper wrote an article refuting this claim with extreme and unrestrained vigor, stating roughly that when the current Emperor (referring to the Russian King) was still the Crown Prince, he had traveled to Japan and was suddenly attacked by Japanese assassins, barely escaping with his life. Furthermore, when Li Wenzhong of China was ordered to go to Maguan, Japan, to negotiate peace, he was also shot by a Japanese person, with the bullet entering his cheek, but fortunately, he did not die. Since the Japanese act with such recklessness, how can their pronouncements be trusted? This matter is recorded in "Feelings of a Trip to Russia" by Zhang Jun Fenghui, which demonstrates that the Japanese fabricating rumors is a long-standing practice, even more rampant now than in the past.
