Narrating Heroes of Our Nation Who Refuse to Surrender Their Lands (Part 1) 159

— Lean Scholar

Some worry about Ma Zhanshan, an isolated army in a remote fortress, saying he is a defeated general facing the ferocious and greedy Japanese army, so how could he be lucky? I say, you are mistaken. Everyone must die. The deaths of Xi Qia and Zhang Haipeng can be called dying for the enemy. If Ma Zhanshan dies from using up all his bullets and having no reinforcements, it can be called dying for the country. Dying for the enemy, even in death, brings eternal ridicule. Dying for the country, though dead, is like being alive, enough to inspire the hearts of those who die later and invigorate the souls of those who have not yet died, to fight the enemy to the very end. Therefore, I examine past events to encourage those in the future and to embolden those who have the responsibility to defend the land.

When I read the Tang Dynasty history about Zhang Xun and Xu Yuan, Yin Ziqi besieged Suiyang. The food in the city was exhausted. Zhang Xun and Xu Yuan discussed, saying, "Suiyang is the shield of the Yangtze and Huai Rivers. If we abandon it, the enemy will certainly take advantage of the victory and advance swiftly, and there will be no more Yangtze and Huai Rivers. Moreover, our troops are hungry and exhausted, and running away will not get us far. It is better to hold our ground and wait for rescue." Therefore, they used tea paper as food. When that was gone, they ate horses. When the horses were gone, they trapped sparrows and dug up rats to eat. When the sparrows and rats were gone, Xun offered his beloved concubine, killing her to feed the soldiers. When the enemy climbed the city walls, the soldiers were too sick to fight. Xun bowed twice to the west and said, "My strength is exhausted. I cannot repay Your Majesty in life, but in death, I will be a vengeful ghost to kill the enemy." The city fell, and Xun and Yuan were both captured. Ziqi said, "I heard that when you fought, your eyes were cracked and your teeth were shattered. Why?" Xun said, "My ambition was to swallow the rebel thieves, but I regret that I lacked the strength to do so." He and his generals Nan Jiyun and Lei Wanchun, along with thirty-six others, were all killed. Initially, when Zhang Xun was besieged, he used the government office as a commander's hall, hanging a portrait of Emperor Gaozu and prostrating himself in tears to encourage the soldiers. His loyalty and bravery were like this.

When Jiang Tianyi Ming Zhang Xianzhong captured Wuchang, General Zuo Liangyu also fled east. At that time, the wolf troops rioted on the road, burning and looting everything they passed. When they were about to reach Hui, the people of Hui were terrified. A secretary named Jin Shengmou went to resist them, entrusting the troops to Tianyi. Tianyi was from Shexian County. Although he was known as a scholar, he was profound, wise, and resourceful. He originally wanted to unite the local people to defend the area. Upon receiving the order, he girded on his sword and set off on horseback in the dark of night, leading brave warriors thousands of miles to fight the rebels in Qimen, beheading the majority and seizing their cattle, horses, and weapons. Hui was thus able to turn danger into safety. In the summer of the second year of the Qing Shunzhi reign, Jiangnan was in turmoil.

Mourning Zhimo 160

— Huang Yanpei

A talent bestowed by heaven, his death is also extraordinary,

A cloud chariot and wind horses evoke his stately appearance.

Thirty years of sorrow and joy, a fleeting spring dream,

Leaving behind a volume of poetry for the world.

The withering willows of Baimen lock in the slanting mist,

The cold drums of the Black Water move the nine borders.

Knowing that there is no place to die in the divine land,

He flew away, chanting, to shed his mortal form in the vast sky.

The crescent moon, slender like a brush,

Is pure but not frivolous, an extraordinary figure.

His radiance connected autumn carriages for ten miles,

Crying until the next of kin, his feelings already private.

To the Tune of "Duoli" (West Lake), Presented to Hai Su 161

— Zhang Sheng

My friend Hai Weng led students from the American Academy of Fine Arts to sketch in West Lake in mid-November, producing more than ten recent works with strong colors and majestic aura. The talent and beautiful scenery complement each other perfectly. I compose this poem to add to it.

I recall the Twin Peaks, leaving behind only returning geese in the vast sea. (Hai Weng returned to China from Europe only a few months ago.) The rain patters, and the boat passes Xiling. Autumn brings a misty artistic mood. I unfurl my nostalgic feelings, poetic spirit, and daring, and imbibe the heavenly charm of the bright moon and red maple leaves. Artistic companions are heroic and extraordinary. The lake light is clear and beautiful, and they murmur their heartfelt feelings by the waves. On the shores of the lonely island, there is a natural painting book, and wonderful thoughts cleanse the chest of dust. I often turn my head to the secluded charm of Nine Streams (Nine Streams and Eighteen Gorges are the most secluded scenes of West Lake) and the immortal traces of Three Peaks.

Looking at the previous dynasty, pens sang and ink danced. I still remember Su Gong's romantic charm. Stirring up bold feelings and the splendor of thousands of springs, moving the unrestrained spirit and the clear bells of ten thousand ages. Clouds are made into clothes, and mountains are used as lapels and belts. Wild geese fall on the horizon, and rainbows appear on the water's edge. To whom can I tell a song of the high mountains? The sea universe sighs at drifting duckweed. I envy the exquisite art of Hu Tou facing the wind, the divine craftsmanship of nature.

The prefectures and counties were falling like dominoes, but the people of Hui still resisted and refused to surrender. In June, the Tang domain established itself in Fuzhou. Upon hearing of Tianyi's name, they appointed him as a supervising judge. Before long, the Qing army attacked Jixi. Tianyi believed that although Hui was a strategically advantageous place, Jixi was flat and stretched out, with only one side facing the main road, so it was necessary to build a pass and gather the people to hold it back. Therefore, they built Congshan Pass. Tianyi led the troops to climb it first every morning and evening, and the enemy was afraid of him. One day, the city fell. The Qing commander urgently sought Tianyi. Tianyi knew that the situation was hopeless. He sent his mother back to Tianbiao, then opened the pass and shouted, "I am Jiang Tianyi!" When some wanted to release him, he said, "Do you think I am afraid of death?" When some said, "Your old mother is still alive, you cannot die," he laughed and said, "How can one who is working with others to save the country cherish his own life?" When he was captured and brought to Jiangning, the guards wanted to kill him. Tianyi opened his mouth and cursed, saying, "If I do not die, I will certainly rise up again with troops. It is better to kill me now." So he was killed under Tongji Gate. Before his execution, he shouted "Long live the Gao Emperor" three times, bowed twice facing south, then stretched out his neck to receive the punishment, regarding death as returning home. Those who saw it could not help but weep and soak their sleeves.

A Groundbreaking New Dictionary Sample 162

— Yun Sheng

"Non-resistance" can be interpreted as "waiting for death with folded hands." This specifically refers to foreign affairs. It does not apply to domestic affairs.

"(Composure)" The character "鎭" (zhen, suppress) is composed of "金" (jin, metal) and "眞" (zhen, true). It means that true gold is not afraid of fire. Let the fire burn as it may. But if the fire is too fierce, even true gold will melt, let alone something that is not true gold. The character "靜" (jing, quiet) is composed of "靑" (qing, blue/green). It means that one can compete under the flag of the Blue Sky and White Sun. Otherwise, it is not allowed. This is what is called "composure."

"(Justice)" As the saying goes, "The public has their reasons, and the women have their reasons." But ultimately, the women's influence is less than the public's. So, the public's reasons are considered just. This is what is called "justice."

"(Thoroughbred Horse)" Horse refers to Ma Zhanshan. It means Ma Zhanshan, who wants to defend the thousands of miles of Heilongjiang land with an isolated army. (Self-Defense) When Country A's troops provoke incidents and arbitrarily massacre in the territory of Country B, it can all be called self-defense. Or when Country B's troops retreat in advance to preserve their strength, it can also be called self-defense. (Overthrow) This is a catchphrase, or used as decoration when written down. It does not mean actually using force.

"(League of Nations)" This refers to the alliance of several imperialists. It cannot be interpreted otherwise.

"(Shenyang)" Shen is interchangeable with Shen (審,审, to examine). Meaning to consider, to know, to understand. Yang is the sun. It means to examine the situation and know that the Japanese army will surely come.

"(Liaoning)" Liao means distant. Ning means peaceful. It means that if the enemy comes, those who defend this land should avoid them from afar in order to live in temporary peace.

"(Economic Severance)" A term relative to political severance. It means that while economic relations are severed, political relations may not be severed. (Republic of China) A term desired by the general patriotic populace. Warlords, bureaucrats, and politicians are not the populace, so it does not concern them and can be sold cheaply or presented with both hands.

I, considering that previous dictionaries are all inapplicable, have compiled this book. I am first issuing a sample page. All those who do not love the country may adopt it. Distribution point: Republic of China Grand Bookstore. Completely free of charge. Not taking a single cent.

A Study on Chrysanthemums That Do and Do Not Fall 163

— Jun Shuo

Yesterday, I passed by my friend Li Junzhai's residence with a guest and saw more than a dozen chrysanthemums displayed under the steps. Those that bloomed earlier, although nearly withered, did not fall. This is the nature of this chrysanthemum. The guest said, "The chrysanthemums of Huangzhou fall," and then recited a poem by a predecessor, saying, "Only the falling petals are from the chrysanthemums of Huangzhou. The expert Jinggong admired Zizhan." This refers to when Wang Jiefu chanted about withered chrysanthemums, "The wind and rain of dusk pass through the garden, blowing golden chrysanthemums all over the ground." Su Zizhan saw this and continued, saying, "Autumn flowers do not fall like spring flowers, I report this to the poet for careful consideration." This offended Jiefu, and Zizhan was exiled to Huangzhou.

Zhimo's Death (4) 164

— Liu Haisu

"Haisu, I've come with two friends to see your paintings," he said. "Let me introduce them. This is Luo Longji. This is Miss Wang."

He himself took out the paintings I had piled on the side one by one and leaned them against the easel. He stood there frankly and looked at them. He looked at them once and talked about them several times. Every time he looked at a painting, he always said "Haisu, Haisu" using the same intimate way he would speak to a sibling. I also unknowingly felt as intimate as my brother returning home. Before long, our friend Gu Yinting came from Nanjing. He greeted Yinting as if unexpectedly meeting after a long separation. It was very natural, as if he had assimilated with nature. He also very enthusiastically called Yinting to look at my paintings. Later, everyone talked about the affairs of the Northeast and the affairs of Florence. He recalled the secrets of Florence, and he also sighed grandly about national affairs. He talked until five o'clock before he left. As he left, he said again. "Haisu, wait a while and come to my house earlier to go to Cheng Linsheng's place together for dinner to see Shi Tao."

Around seven o'clock, I arrived at Zhimo's house. He was shouting madly upstairs again. After sitting for a moment, Wang Wenbai also came. He brought up the matter of looking at the paintings one by one, and urged Wenbai to go and see my paintings quickly. Wenbai always dealt with him with a smile.

After a while, we went to Cheng's house. Walking into the house, the Japanese led the way all the way to the living room. But Mr. Cheng had not yet returned home. There were only three middle-aged gentlemen or wealthy merchants. Later, Mr. Weng led us to see the bronzes in Mr. Cheng's collection, and there were quite a few rare ones. After Mr. Cheng returned, he had a long talk with me about Shi Tao. Zhimo just listened quietly.

During the meal, they talked a lot about Chinese paintings and calligraphy. Mr. Cheng was very respectful to us. He and Wenbai also talked about the current economic situation in Shanghai. I am very ignorant of this passage, so I have forgotten it completely.

After the meal, we were full of hope. We hoped to see Shi Tao soon.

When Mr. Cheng unfolded Shi Tao's "Hundred Beauties" large scroll, we all stopped talking. We just watched carefully. After reading the "Hundred Beauties", we also read a dozen other hand scrolls in a row. There were landscape paintings, ink orchids, ink chrysanthemums, and Arhats. We looked at them until twelve o'clock.

"Excellent, excellent" we said in unison.

At this time, Zhu Qinglan and Cha Mianzhong came again. They also talked a lot about the affairs of Heilongjiang and disaster relief. Mr. Zhu is a real philanthropist. He is really able to petition for the people in disaster. His prestige is also very great. I think. In the past thirty years in China. There has never been such a person who can make people feel grateful. Mianzhong has also left the education business in recent years. Following Mr. Zhu to help disaster relief. Because China is a country of disasters.

"It's not early. It's about one o'clock. Don't just keep pestering me and not want to leave." I said this. So I, Zhimo and Wenbai said goodbye to the host and left the house.

. Only the chrysanthemums of Huangzhou shed their petals. Zizhan saw this and was greatly ashamed. Mr. Li then said that this incident was Ou Gong, not Su Zizhan. Jiefu chanted about withered chrysanthemums, and Ouyang Yongshu playfully continued with the line "Autumn flowers do not fall like spring flowers." Jiefu heard this and laughed, saying, "Ou Jiu is ignorant. Haven't you seen the Chu Ci has 'eating the falling petals of autumn chrysanthemums at dusk'?" I then remembered that I had seen this matter in the book "Yunlang Oubi" written by Song Muzhong. It said that he was an official in Huangzhou for several years and planted many chrysanthemums, but he had never seen any petals fall. He also examined the Huangzhou Zhi and various books on Huangzhou's customs and products, and there was no record of Zizhan seeing chrysanthemum petals fall. This is suspected to be a popular saying and not credible. However, after examining the postscript to a certain chrysanthemum manual, it says that some chrysanthemums fall and some do not. It is said that those with tightly packed petals do not fall. If the petals are sparse, after full bloom, they gradually become scattered. When shaken by wind and rain, they scatter all over the ground. Now, according to this statement, it is more credible. Due to the difference between sparse and tightly packed, there is a distinction between falling and not falling. However, if it does not encounter wind and rain shaking, even if the sparse petals are scattered, they will surely dry up and not fall quickly. This is true of chrysanthemums everywhere, not necessarily only in Huangzhou. Or it is said that the "falling petals" in the Chu Ci "falling petals of autumn chrysanthemums" should be interpreted as "beginning". Erya, "Chu Luo Quanyu" means "beginning." The "falling" in the Mao Shi also means "beginning." Therefore, it is said that the initial bloom of chrysanthemums is fragrant and lovely. After they wither, how can there be any flavor to eat? This understanding is also appropriate. However, the two characters "falling petals" are used in other books and cannot be enumerated. There is no one who uses it to mean the beginning of a flower. What is wrong with eating the falling petals of chrysanthemums to express the meaning of loneliness and purity? My friend Mr. Li also said that those with tightly packed petals do not fall, and sparse and scattered petals cannot withstand the shaking of wind and rain. Hearing this sentence, it is even more sad for our country, which is now being horizontally invaded and humiliated. Alas!

After Economic Severance with Japan 169

(1) Jianping

The magnitude of the effect can be known

Since the violent Japanese occupied my Liaoji region from September 18th, it has aroused the nationwide boycott of Japanese goods and economic severance with Japanese people in our country. For more than two months, it has caused Japanese businessmen in China to be on the verge of ruin, and the foreign trade of inferior goods, which has always regarded China as its only market, has also been fundamentally broken. Japan's trade with China is nothing less than the source of its national life. Once our country economically severs ties with it, Japan's national industries will be affected. It is not only a part of Japanese expatriate merchants in China, but also Japan's initial entire exports, which have always regarded China as their main market. No matter silk fabrics, cotton fabrics, large and small hardware, as well as various toys, utensils, sugar, and seafood, none of them account for the majority of sales in China. Therefore, inside the Yangtze River, from Xulu, Chengdu, and Chongqing in Sichuan, down to Zhenning and Suzhou in Jiangsu Province, and along the river in southern and northern Anhui, Xunbu in Jiangxi Province, and Wuhan and Shayi in central Hubei, and even Changsha, Xiangtan, Changde, and Dongting in central Hunan, almost no place that can be reached by water and land is without the footprints of Japanese people. Wherever Japanese people arrive, Japanese goods are popularized to the inland. Even remote and poor villages are subject to their economic aggression. Not to mention the major trading ports. Whether it is household necessities or everyday needs in our country, all of them are replaced by Japanese goods. In ordinary families, in terms of the problem of food, there are bowls and dishes made of oriental porcelain. In terms of the problem of clothing, there are Japanese broadcloth and various silk fabrics and satin. In terms of the problem of utensils, there are Japanese umbrellas and other miscellaneous goods. Among the public goods of the society, there are even oil ink, paper, pens, hardware, rubber products, and other items. To the extreme, it can be said that from copper and iron to matches and sewing needles, there is nothing that is not available. Moreover, with low water transportation costs and light taxes, all goods coming to China are bound by unequal treaties and cannot increase their tax rates. Moreover, with the subsidies from their government, the costs can be cheapened and compete with the imported goods from other countries in China. They can naturally occupy a superior position. Furthermore, due to the sluggishness of China's industries and the immaturity of its businesses, the quality of its products is poor. As a result, the sales of Japanese goods in China have become even greater, and their trade with China has become increasingly developed.

In the second year of the Republic of China, Japanese people obtained the rights to five railway lines in Manchuria and Mongolia. As a result, the commerce in the Northeast was completely monopolized by them. When the European War broke out, the Japanese people took advantage of this opportunity to consolidate their rights in Manchuria and Mongolia and further seize the economic rights of the entire Shandong Province. The Twenty-One Demands were forced upon us for recognition, arousing the unanimous opposition of our country, which once boycotted Japanese goods, but it soon subsided. When the May 3rd Jinan Massacre occurred in the seventeenth year, it also aroused resistance and boycott, but it disappeared invisibly not long after. This time, the troops occupied our three eastern provinces, and the number of people killed and the gold and silver plundered cannot be calculated in numbers. Our country has a non-resistant military authority, and the people can only use economic severance as a weapon of self-defense. The Japanese pirates are not afraid of our military force, nor are they afraid of our resistance, but what they fear is the economic severance carried out by our country. The effect of the boycott is enough to put the financial lifeline of the Japanese pirates in a desperate situation. If the people of our country can be of one mind, determined and unyielding, and support the boycott of Japanese goods for one or two years, no matter how sharp the guns and cannons of the Japanese pirates are, they will only end up with exhausted finances and a weak country, and our final victory will only be possible by controlling the enemy to death through boycott and returning triumphantly. I hope that the people of our country will not be slack. The strength or weakness of the country and the survival of the nation depend on whether this economic severance can be upheld or not. Regarding the damage suffered by the Japanese pirates after the boycott, I will describe the general situation in sections below.

(1) Expatriate Businessmen Eliminated Everywhere 170

From the time the violent Japanese occupied our Northeast on September 18th to September 23rd, the people of the Yangtze River ports immediately rose up to effectively boycott Japanese goods. The initial mobilization started in Shanghai when the Wanbaoshan incident had just begun and Liaoji fell. The provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan responded in unison, severing economic ties with Japanese merchants. At first, trade was suspended, then inferior goods were inspected, and finally all industries were severed. From October 16th, the Yangtze River Basin, which the Japanese regard as deeply rooted in economic aggression in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, was fundamentally plunged into despair. In Chengdu, Chongqing, Xulu, Wanxian, and other ports in Sichuan, as well as Yichang and Shashi, Japanese merchants not only could not conduct business, but also faced obstacles in purchasing food. As a result, the Japanese merchants in the upper Yangtze River closed their businesses and withdrew from the Yangtze River Basin, moving to Shanghai. By late October, Japanese merchants in Xiang and E ports had also closed their businesses one after another. The Japanese Qing dispatched two ships to transport these Japanese expatriates to Shanghai. At the same time, the Japanese in Jiujiang, Wuhu, Daye, Anqing, and Nanjing and Zhenjiang followed suit and stopped operations, all arriving in Shanghai in late October and early November. A total of more than 800 people arrived in Shanghai one after another. Their women and children had already taken ships back to their country, while the men left some people in Shanghai. In mid-November, Japanese expatriates in Suzhou, Wenzhou, Shantou in Fujian, and Guangdong also withdrew from various ports due to the fierce boycott, going to Cai Long, coming to Shanghai, or returning directly to Dongyang. The businesses of Japanese merchants in various inland areas and the Yangtze River Basin, Nanhua, and other ports have been almost completely eliminated. What remains and has not been withdrawn is only the major ports of Shanghai and Tianjin. Since the Tianjin incident, 600 Japanese expatriates have seized four Japanese ships and will also withdraw, it is said.

(II) Special Products Plummet 171

Dalian Bay is the only seaport for Japan to transport goods through Manchuria and Mongolia. Most of the goods of the South Manchuria Railway are shipped from here. From October of the fifth year of the Showa era (1930) to May of the sixth year (1931), the amount of soybeans exported from Dalian Port totaled 350,000 tons, which was a significant decrease compared to the previous year. The quantities of soybean cakes, soybean oil, sorghum, and other items also gradually declined. The main reason is that the new railways built in the three northeastern provinces have gradually succeeded in encircling the South Manchuria Railway. Once Huludao Port is successfully opened, the export trade of Dalian Bay will be entirely taken back by our country's railways. Japan's all-out efforts to manage and invade Manchuria and Mongolia will be fundamentally broken. The September 18th Incident (Mukden Incident) was probably a desperate measure. According to investigations, before the new railways in our eastern provinces were fully completed a year ago, various special products were transported through Dalian Port. After completion, the amount exported decreased significantly, mostly diverted and loaded from Yingkou. The comparison of special products is as follows:

The total reduction of the above goods compared to the previous year is 15,809 tons. Once Huludao is completed, Dalian will have even less transportation.

(III) Japanese Goods Shipped to China Greatly Reduced 172

Japan's foreign trade relies on China as its largest market, taking our raw materials and shipping manufactured goods. Japanese goods shipped to China were most prosperous in the 15th year of the Republic (1926). Since the 16th year (1927), due to the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army and the inclusion of the areas north and south of the Yangtze River into military zones, the market for Japanese goods has inevitably decreased slightly. It is found that Japanese goods shipped to our country in peacetime are mainly piece goods, cotton yarn, sugar, seafood, and other toys. In 1927, the value of goods shipped to the Northeast was 161 million yuan; in 1929, it was 215 million yuan. The value of goods shipped to North China was 103 million yuan in 1927 and 76 million yuan in 1929. The value of goods shipped to South China was 282 million yuan in 1927 and 216 million yuan in 1929. The total was 546 million yuan in 1927 and 507 million yuan in 1929. This time, the resistance to goods can be called a unanimous mobilization of the industrial, commercial, and people of the whole country. The northeastern provinces have completely stopped purchasing due to the military incidents, and North China has also successively, from September,

Page 16

stopped signing purchase contracts with Japanese merchants. Those who have already come to Shanghai are strictly prohibited from unloading by the Anti-Japanese Association. The goods that have already come to Shanghai cannot be transshipped and are accumulated to a great extent. Those that were scheduled to come to Shanghai have all failed to depart. From September to today, the Chinese and Japanese ships of the postal company have reduced the number of ships due to lack of goods to load. The Japanese imports to China that have arrived in recent days only include some Japanese stones and Western paper. In addition, the large-volume goods of some time ago, such as piece goods, yarn, sugar, and seafood, are not loaded at all. According to statistics from Japanese commercial officials in Shanghai, since the Wanbaoshan Incident in July to the present, Japan's trade with China has decreased by 76 million yuan in exports alone, and the value of Japanese gold shipments has also decreased by 18 million yuan. If we combine the national estimates, this resistance has caused Japanese goods coming to China to decrease by more than 150 million yuan, and the raw materials shipped from China have also decreased by more than 37 million yuan. The resistance of five months has been like this. If we calculate the annual total, the amount of Japanese goods shipped to China will decrease by 180 million yuan annually. According to Japanese gold calculations, the figures for trade with China have actually been completely wiped out, and its economic impact is sufficient to trigger its enormous terror.

(IV) Japanese Coal Has No Market at All 173

The sales of Japanese coal in China in 1928 totaled 1.49 million tons shipped to China for sale, and in 1929, it totaled 1.33 million tons. This year, the Kailuan Coal Mine experienced a shutdown, and Shanghai suddenly faced a coal shortage. Japanese coal took the opportunity to enter the market, and the sales of Fushun coal in Shanghai were unprecedentedly smooth and in high demand. According to last year, the amount of Japanese coal shipped to China was 1,319,000 tons. At that time, Fushun coal lump No. 1 was 13.5 yuan, and No. 2 was 12.2 yuan, while Kailuan coal No. 2 screened lump was only 9.7 yuan. During the most prosperous period, Japanese coal in Shanghai was in such short supply that Mitsui, Mitsubishi, and others chartered more than 30 large Chinese, British, and Norwegian cargo ships to transport Japanese coal to Shanghai to meet the demand, and the sales market for Japanese coal increased by more than 150,000 tons per month. By September of this year, the amount of Japanese coal shipped to China had reached 2 million tons, and the Shanghai coal market had been manipulated by the Japanese. However, after the September 18th Incident, the Chinese unanimously decided not to purchase Japanese coal, and the organizing committee implemented a cessation of purchases. Since October, all factories, fields, and commercial ships have uniformly switched to using domestic coal. More than 60 coal ships of Mitsubishi, Mitsui, Dalian, and others have simultaneously stopped sailing since November, and the Ministry of Communications has heeded the request of state-owned coal mines and has not ordered the Shanghai Shipping Company to specially dispatch eight ships to Qingdao and its surrounding areas to transport domestic coal to supply factories and ships. If we can persevere to the end, the annual loss of Japanese coal shipped to China will be 26 million yuan, or more than 50 million yuan in Japanese gold converted to national currency. (To be continued)

Social News Submission Guidelines 174

(1) The text should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas (2) hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life news and white pictures should be limited to various lyrical paintings about social life. (3) Photographs of seasonal, scenery, animals and plants, people, and news photography are acceptable. Photographs of fashionable women in seasonal landscapes are especially welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(5) Do not write horizontally, and do not write sloppily. Western text should be omitted where possible. If it is necessary to use it, the original text must be attached below the translation.

Art World

Paris Literary Reporters Association Holds Louis Veuillot Centenary Memorial 175

— Luo Hansu

October 30th of this year marks the 100th anniversary of the death of Louis Veuillot, a great modern French writer. On this day, the deceased's family and friends, along with the French Literary Reporters Association, jointly initiated a memorial service to commemorate this strong figure in the literary world, literary reporter, Catholic, and loyal writer of France from a century ago.

At 10 a.m., a memorial mass was held at the Saint-Thomas-d'Aquin Church in Paris. Louis Veuillot's descendants and relatives all attended the religious and solemn ceremony.

A moving poem, Louis Veuillot's will, was inserted into the musical program:

"Please place this scroll at my feet,

And gently close my coffin."

Notable among the relatives and guests were Mrs. General Bi Ai Long, Louis Veuillot's daughter; Mr. François Veuillot, the deceased's nephew; Mr. Gao Yao, President of the Louis Veuillot Friends Association; Mr. Gao Feiai, representative of the French Academy; General Castex; members of parliament; poets; novelists; and many literary reporters.

First, Father Chanoine, the parish priest of Saint-Thomas-d'Aquin Church, delivered a short speech. After the religious ceremony, a cornerstone laying ceremony was held at Louis Veuillot's death residence, 21 Rue de Varenne.

Mr. Gao Yao spoke on behalf of the Veuillot Friends Association. Mr. Gao Yao delivered a very ornate eulogy to the great Catholic literary reporter who had already died. He praised Louis Veuillot as "a Catholic Voltaire, but a Voltaire with both emotion and conscience."

Finally, Mr. François Veuillot recalled his uncle's death throes at the Rue de Varenne residence: "An old soldier of Catholicism made his last struggle here, fulfilling his duty to defend religion."

At 6 p.m., a rich and grand banquet was prepared, attended by well-known figures in the Paris art and literature circles and important figures in the religious world.

During the banquet, guests gave speeches one after another, among which the speech by Bishop Fan Nessa, an expert in the study of Veuillot's life and works, was the most popular. The guests and hosts dispersed joyfully in the middle of the night.

World-Renowned Violinist Heifetz Recital 176

— Zhang Ruogu

Among the most famous first-class violinists in today's world music scene, there are several that can be counted: Zimbalist, Szigeti, and Elman are two stars in the Northern European violin world; Kreisler is a master produced by Vienna and Paris; Thibaud is a famous French violinist. All four of them are disciples of the famous Hungarian violin teacher Auer. They have now all gained fame and are traveling the world on musical pilgrimages. They have almost all been to Shanghai to dedicate their artistic skills. Recently, another world-renowned violinist, Heifetz, held his first recital in Shanghai at the New Light Grand Theater.

Heifetz is a musical prodigy. He knows how to cherish his prodigy talent and does not abandon himself because of the easily obtained early fame, nor does he indulge in vanity and arrogant tricks in his youth like other artists.

Most music lovers like to compare the strengths and weaknesses of various famous musicians and even like to rank them. This is originally a meaningless game because violinists like Kreisler, Thibaud, Elman, and Heifetz have all achieved the status of first-class musical masters, and there is originally no such thing as first and last or first and second. They themselves are standing on a horizontal line above the same level. However, the audience inevitably has subjective observations and must, of course, make praises and criticisms.

If you want me to give a concise judgment on the violinists mentioned above, then I can only tell you that Kreisler is a musician of the ancient style, Thibaud is a seductive artist, Elman is a wanderer, and Heifetz is a master of musical rhythm. From the appearance, we can tell at a glance that Heifetz is a master of musical rhythm. Look at his straight posture when he takes the stage, as if he is sacred and inviolable. His facial expression is calm and there are no unnatural expressions. Many people say he is too indifferent, which is a superficial observation. I would like those audiences who specialize in watching facial grimaces or frivolous actions to close their eyes, concentrate their minds, and listen quietly. You will naturally feel Heifetz's melody, his excitement, and his liveliness. He is by no means an indifferent person. His musical rhythm is not mechanical. He has his special talent. He is a musical master. The program he played in his first recital (November 20th) was very brilliant. Vitali's "Ancient Dance Suite - La Chaconne" was very fresh and sparkling. Lalo's "Spanish Symphony" was very elegant and also very beautiful and smooth. The second part included masterpieces by Bach, Debussy, De Falla, and Ravel.

Heifetz is Heifetz. He has his special authority. He has the priority that others do not have. His technique sometimes pulls him too far away. On the whole, the music he played on the first night could fully express the essence of each work to the best of its ability. Bach's "Lament" is a classical work. Debussy's "The Girl with the Flaxen Hair" and De Falla's Jota are both full of Latin style. Although they lack the generosity and moderation of the classical school, they have also shed the tenderness and beauty of France and Spain, but they have a sense of evenness in the blending of light and shade.

Anyone who has heard Heifetz's first recital will definitely retain these beautiful impressions in their memories for a long time. La Chaconne sang the lively waltz, Ravel's "Wandering Song" sobbed sadly, and Lalo's "Scherzo" emitted a very light and decisive sparkling light.

The pianist Achron's playing technique was very expressive, but unfortunately the audience could not hear it clearly, especially when accompanying the "Spanish Symphony," he played too softly.

Literary Anecdotes

Recent News from the London Publishing World 177

— An Ping

"Do men buy books?"

Page 22

This question was recently raised by a reporter from a London newspaper because the reporter said that according to a report from a friend in the book industry, all the customers buying books in London recently are women.

A man can spend a pound without hesitation on small drinks, small snacks, or in the theater, but when it comes to taking out a few shillings to buy books, he seems unwilling. But in the same newspaper that published this question, they made a broad solicitation to the London book industry in their own newspaper. As a result, there was a fair explanation for whether men buy books and whether men are stingy with their money when buying books. Although the reports from the bookstores said that most of the customers who come to buy books are women, they also reported that these customers have different interests in buying books. They said that generally, when a man buys books, he always buys some useful books. Their attitude towards buying books is very serious. If they really want to buy, then the amount spent is greater than that of women. Most women buy books just to casually buy some to pass the time, while men love to buy some permanently useful books that are permanently worth putting on their shelves.

The Croydon Public Library in London makes a detailed report on its annual book supply statistics every year. According to this year's report, it seems that the demand for reading and borrowing those stimulating and easily arousing novels is very small among the books borrowed out each year. The readership of war works has also fallen sharply. Only classical books still maintain their original position, probably because the masses are too tired and bored of war. But on the one hand, although this is the case, books on war history and other categories still have a considerable market. Winston Churchill wrote in the fifth volume of "The World Crisis" published in 1929: "The materials in this volume were almost all collected by me within ten years and have many of the freshest contributions to the history of the last war." The publishing company of this book announced that it plans to continue with another sequel, a sequel of 130,000 words. This sequel may be called "The Unknown War," writing about matters on the Eastern Front.

The twelfth and final volume, the thirteenth volume, of "The Medical History of the War" published by the Stationary Office will also be published soon. This is compiled by the official side, and another book "The Fifth Army" written by General Hebegu may cause a stir for a while because this book will reveal all the most important inside stories. In terms of content, there are many places that involve the reputation of some high-ranking politicians and military personnel.

There are still many books of this kind to be published, such as Plain's "In the Life of War," etc., now in the London publishing world.

Following war novels, the most active books in the London publishing world are biographies. Many people are discussing this issue more vigorously than discussing all literary issues. Professor Blair is compiling a great dictionary of national biographies. Shatai Lee said that literary success must have something unusual to show in the book. Today's biographical works are generally too ordinary. Many people are becoming interested in these works. Readers buy them regardless of whether these things are worth reading, and they keep buying them one by one.

A female writer, Jameson, told people that she can only write 500 words a day, from 9:30 in the morning to 7:30 in the afternoon. Excluding the time for eating in these ten hours, if each hour is divided, then 50 words are not enough to calculate. She is the smallest and slowest writer.

Recent News from the New York Publishing World 178

— An Ping

Simon & Schuster will publish a biography about George Bernard Shaw in October of this year. This book is written by Frank Harris and is considered to be the most brilliant biography of the season. This book will completely collect Shaw's life's work and his writings. The author said that in this book, he will tell you all the truth about Shaw. The materials collected in this book are very new and have letters and other pictures and photos directly written by Shaw to the author, it is said.
